# Salish Sea Dreaming -- Data Map

**Interactive knowledge graph for the Salish Sea Dreaming AI art installation**

- **Exhibition:** Digital Ecologies: Bridging Nature and Technology
- **Venue:** Mahon Hall, Salt Spring Island, BC
- **Dates:** April 10--26, 2026
- **Creator:** Salish Sea Dreaming Collective
- **License:** Mixed -- see per-asset licenses
- **Date Published:** 2026-04-10


## The Exhibition

Digital Ecologies: Bridging Nature and Technology — Salt Spring Art Show at Mahon Hall, April 10–26, 2026.

### Digital Ecologies
Type: installation | Tier: 0

An interactive AI art installation exploring the Salish Sea ecosystem. The vision: not humans looking at nature through technology, but the Salish Sea using technology to perceive itself. Curated by Raf for the Digital Ecologies show.

Connections: -> The Salish Sea (conceptual), -> Artists & Witnesses (conceptual), -> Training Corpus (conceptual), -> The Dreaming Machine (conceptual), -> Visitor Dreams (conceptual), -> Knowledge & Research (conceptual), <- The Exhibition (contains), <- Digital Ecologies: Mediating More-Than-Human Worlds (conceptual)

### Carol Anne Hilton
Type: person | Tier: 1

Indigenomics founder, vision holder. Framework for relational value and Indigenous economic design.

Connections: <- The Exhibition (contains)

### Natalia Lebedinskaia
Type: person | Tier: 1

Panel moderation and contextual framing.

Connections: <- The Exhibition (contains)

### Pravin Pillay
Type: person | Tier: 1

Creative Director (MOVE37XR). TouchDesigner, AI visualization, immersive media. Studio: 108 Fraser Rd, Salt Spring.

Connections: <- The Exhibition (contains)

### Raf
Type: person | Tier: 1

Curator, Digital Ecologies exhibition at Mahon Hall.

Connections: <- The Exhibition (contains)


## The Salish Sea

The Salish Sea ecosystem — a living web of salmon, herring, orca, kelp, and hundreds of interconnected species. The Five Threads weave through it.

### Herring
Type: concept | Tier: 0

Pacific herring are the foundation of the Salish Sea food web. Their spawning events — turning the water milky white — feed hundreds of species. DFO management set baselines from 1953, a year that was already catastrophic. Indigenous nations like the Heiltsuk challenged this, taking over their own stock assessment.

Connections: -> Salmon & Forage Fish (conceptual), -> HerringFest (conceptual), -> Pacific Herring (conceptual), -> Herring Spawn (conceptual), <- The Salish Sea (contains)

### Orca
Type: concept | Tier: 0

The Southern Resident orca pods (J, K, and L) are a family in crisis. Down to ~75 individuals, they face starvation from depleted Chinook salmon, toxic bioaccumulation, and vessel noise. Tahlequah (J35) carried her dead calf for 17 days in 2018 — a mourning procession witnessed around the world.

Connections: -> Marine Mammals (conceptual), -> Moonfish Footage (conceptual), -> Orca (conceptual), -> Whale Underwater (conceptual), <- The Salish Sea (contains)

### Salmon
Type: concept | Tier: 0

The salmon thread traces the great cycle — ocean to river to forest and back. Salmon carry marine nutrients deep into the watershed, feeding eagles, bears, and ancient cedars. Their return is the pulse of the coast.

Connections: -> Salmon & Forage Fish (conceptual), -> Moonfish Footage (conceptual), -> Chinook Salmon (conceptual), -> Coho Salmon (conceptual), -> Sockeye Salmon (conceptual), -> Pink Salmon (conceptual), -> Chum Salmon (conceptual), <- The Salish Sea (contains)

### Camas
Type: concept | Tier: 1

Camas meadows were tended by Coast Salish peoples for millennia — burned, harvested, replanted. Colonization disrupted these relationships. Today, camas restoration projects are healing the land and rebuilding reciprocal care. The camas thread is about what grows back when we tend it.

Connections: -> Knowledge & Research (conceptual), <- The Salish Sea (contains)

### Cedar
Type: concept | Tier: 1

Cedar represents deep time. A single western red cedar can live over a thousand years. Cedar is the tree of life for Coast Salish peoples — canoes, longhouses, regalia, medicine. The cedar thread asks: what does it mean to plan on a thousand-year timescale?

Connections: -> Knowledge & Research (conceptual), <- The Salish Sea (contains)


## Artists & Witnesses

The artists and witnesses whose eyes, cameras, and brushes became the project’s sensory organs. Their work is the raw perception.

### Brad Necyk
Type: person | Tier: 1

Artist and researcher, latent space concepts.

Connections: <- Artists & Witnesses (contains)

### Briony Penn
Type: person | Tier: 1

Naturalist, illustrator — watercolors and ecological storytelling. Her art is the visual language of the Salish Sea.

Connections: -> Briony Penn Archive (contains), <- Artists & Witnesses (contains)

### Briony Penn Archive
Type: cluster-summary | Tier: 1

519 paintings, illustrations, and field journals from Briony Penn’s decades of natural history work. Source material for the Briony LoRA style transfer model.

Connections: <- Artists & Witnesses (contains), <- Briony Penn (contains)

### David Denning
Type: person | Tier: 1

Photographer — long-term bioregional witnessing. 14 high-resolution photos used with collaborator permission.

Connections: -> Denning Photos (contains), <- Artists & Witnesses (contains)

### Denning Photos
Type: cluster-summary | Tier: 1

14 high-resolution photographs of Salish Sea coastline, intertidal zones, forests. Long-term bioregional witnessing.

Connections: -> Training Corpus (training), <- Artists & Witnesses (contains), <- David Denning (contains)

### Eve Marenghi
Type: person | Tier: 1

Data scientist, Regen Commons steward. HerringFest documentation.

Connections: -> HerringFest (contains), <- Artists & Witnesses (contains)

### HerringFest
Type: cluster-summary | Tier: 1

65 documentary images from HerringFest on Salt Spring Island — community celebration of Pacific herring. Documented by Eve Marenghi.

Connections: <- Herring (conceptual), <- Artists & Witnesses (contains), <- Eve Marenghi (contains)

### Moonfish Footage
Type: cluster-summary | Tier: 1

13 underwater videos of herring spawning, salmon migration, marine habitats. 416 frames extracted. Layer 1 of the projection uses this footage cross-faded with ControlNet+LoRA style-transferred versions.

Connections: -> Training Corpus (training), <- Salmon (conceptual), <- Orca (conceptual), <- Artists & Witnesses (contains), <- Moonfish Media (contains)

### Moonfish Media
Type: person | Tier: 1

Underwater cinematography team capturing herring, salmon, and marine habitats. 13 videos, 416 frames used with collaborator permission.

Connections: -> Moonfish Footage (contains), <- Artists & Witnesses (contains)


## Training Corpus

1,255 images across 50 species — the visual corpus that trained the Dreaming GAN. Every image is CC-licensed or used with permission.

### Bears
Type: cluster-summary | Tier: 1

1 items in this collection.

### Aggregating Anemone
Type: photo | Tier: 3

This photograph of Aggregating Anemone was part of the training corpus for the Dreaming GAN — the AI model that powers the Salish Sea Dreaming installation at Mahon Hall. Photographed by Davefoc. Source: Openverse. License: CC-BY-SA. Along with 1,254 other images across 50 species, this photo taught the machine to dream in the visual language of the Salish Sea.

Connections: <- Aggregating Anemone (contains)

### Aggregating Anemone
Type: photo | Tier: 3

This photograph of Aggregating Anemone was part of the training corpus for the Dreaming GAN — the AI model that powers the Salish Sea Dreaming installation at Mahon Hall. Photographed by Ed Bierman from CA, usa. Source: Openverse. License: CC-BY. Along with 1,254 other images across 50 species, this photo taught the machine to dream in the visual language of the Salish Sea.

This photograph of Bull Kelp was part of the training corpus for the Dreaming GAN — the AI model that powers the Salish Sea Dreaming installation at Mahon Hall. Photographed by Bernard Spragg. Source: Openverse. License: CC0. Along with 1,254 other images across 50 species, this photo taught the machine to dream in the visual language of the Salish Sea.

This photograph of Common Loon was part of the training corpus for the Dreaming GAN — the AI model that powers the Salish Sea Dreaming installation at Mahon Hall. Photographed by ayatana_biophilium. Source: iNaturalist. License: CC-BY. Along with 1,254 other images across 50 species, this photo taught the machine to dream in the visual language of the Salish Sea.

This photograph of Herring Spawn was part of the training corpus for the Dreaming GAN — the AI model that powers the Salish Sea Dreaming installation at Mahon Hall. Photographed by Braden J. Judson. Source: Openverse. License: CC0. Along with 1,254 other images across 50 species, this photo taught the machine to dream in the visual language of the Salish Sea.

Connections: <- Herring Spawn (contains)

This photograph of Kelp was part of the training corpus for the Dreaming GAN — the AI model that powers the Salish Sea Dreaming installation at Mahon Hall. Along with 1,254 other images across 50 species, this photo taught the machine to dream in the visual language of the Salish Sea.

This photograph of Opalescent Nudibranch was part of the training corpus for the Dreaming GAN — the AI model that powers the Salish Sea Dreaming installation at Mahon Hall. Photographed by jrfrey. Source: iNaturalist. License: CC-BY. Along with 1,254 other images across 50 species, this photo taught the machine to dream in the visual language of the Salish Sea.

This photograph of Orca was part of the training corpus for the Dreaming GAN — the AI model that powers the Salish Sea Dreaming installation at Mahon Hall. Photographed by Gregory 'Slobirdr' Smith. Source: Openverse. License: CC-BY-SA. Along with 1,254 other images across 50 species, this photo taught the machine to dream in the visual language of the Salish Sea.

This photograph of Red Rock Crab was part of the training corpus for the Dreaming GAN — the AI model that powers the Salish Sea Dreaming installation at Mahon Hall. Photographed by Carolyn Prentice. Source: Openverse. License: CC0. Along with 1,254 other images across 50 species, this photo taught the machine to dream in the visual language of the Salish Sea.

Connections: <- Red Rock Crab (contains)

This photograph of Western Grebe was part of the training corpus for the Dreaming GAN — the AI model that powers the Salish Sea Dreaming installation at Mahon Hall. Photographed by sorrykb. Source: iNaturalist. License: CC-BY. Along with 1,254 other images across 50 species, this photo taught the machine to dream in the visual language of the Salish Sea.

## The Dreaming Machine

The dreaming machine. Three projection layers: L1 = Moonfish footage cross-faded with ControlNet+LoRA style-transferred versions. L2 = StreamDiffusion real-time watercolor at 30fps. L3 = Raw Autolume GAN dreams. All composited in Resolume Arena onto the 8×8 ft wall.

### Autolume
Type: artifact | Tier: 1

SFU MetaCreation Lab. Real-time latent space navigation. Audio-reactive, OSC. Layer 3 of projection: raw GAN dreams. Also feeds StreamDiffusion as img2img input.

Connections: -> TouchDesigner (signal), <- The Dreaming Machine (contains), <- Dreaming GAN (signal)

### Boids SOP
Type: td-internal | Tier: 1

Intent field — flocking fish simulation

Connections: <- TouchDesigner (contains)

### Briony LoRA
Type: artifact | Tier: 1

LoRA rank 16, 22 watercolors, SD 1.5. Used in L1 (briony_video_style.py + RAFT smoothing) and L2 (StreamDiffusion real-time). Prompt: "brionypenn watercolor painting, Pacific Northwest coastal ecosystem".

Connections: -> StreamDiffusion (training-lora), <- The Dreaming Machine (contains), <- Briony Training Set (training-lora)

### Briony Training Set
Type: cluster-summary | Tier: 1

22 items in this collection.

Connections: -> Briony LoRA (training-lora), <- The Dreaming Machine (contains)

### Dreaming GAN
Type: artifact | Tier: 1

StyleGAN2-ada (320 kimg), ~1,255 images of 49 species. Abstract organic textures. Dual role: direct projection via Autolume + input to StreamDiffusion.

Connections: -> Autolume (signal), <- Darren Zal (conceptual), <- The Dreaming Machine (contains), <- Salmon & Forage Fish (training), <- Marine Mammals (training), <- Seabirds (training), <- Kelp & Seagrass (training), <- Intertidal (training), <- Cephalopods (training), <- Rockfish & Reef (training)
  ...and 2 more

### Gallery Server
Type: software | Tier: 1

FastAPI server. Processes visitor text through GPT-4.1-mini for content filtering. OSC to TouchDesigner. SQLite for submissions. SSE for live updates.

Connections: -> TouchDesigner (visitor-signal), <- Darren Zal (conceptual), <- The Dreaming Machine (contains), <- QR Portal (visitor-signal), <- Visitor Dreams (visitor-signal)

### Kinect CHOP
Type: td-internal | Tier: 1

Presence and depth sensing

Connections: <- TouchDesigner (contains)

### NDI In TOP
Type: td-internal | Tier: 1

Receives Autolume video feed

Connections: -> StreamDiffusion TOX (signal), <- TouchDesigner (contains)

### OSC In DAT
Type: td-internal | Tier: 1

Receives visitor prompts from gallery server

Connections: -> Prompt Sequencer (signal), <- TouchDesigner (contains)

### Output TOP
Type: td-internal | Tier: 1

Final composite to projector

Connections: <- TouchDesigner (contains), <- StreamDiffusion TOX (signal)

### Projection
Type: output | Tier: 1

The key node. 8×8 ft wall. Three layers in Resolume Arena: L1=Moonfish footage cross-faded with same footage through SD 1.5 + Briony LoRA + ControlNet depth (20 steps). L2=StreamDiffusion real-time watercolor. L3=Raw Autolume GAN.

Connections: <- The Dreaming Machine (contains), <- StreamDiffusion (signal)

### Prompt Sequencer
Type: td-internal | Tier: 1

Cycles 23 ecological prompts (26s each, 6s crossfade). Visitor dreams interrupt for 30s with smooth fade.

Connections: -> StreamDiffusion TOX (signal), <- TouchDesigner (contains), <- OSC In DAT (signal)

### QR Portal
Type: interface | Tier: 1

Scan QR → phone browser → type/speak → 30s on projection wall.

Connections: -> Gallery Server (visitor-signal), <- The Dreaming Machine (contains)

### StreamDiffusion
Type: artifact | Tier: 1

30fps img2img with SD-Turbo inside TD. Takes Autolume GAN output + 23 cycling prompts. Layer 2: real-time watercolor via Briony LoRA. Visitor dreams interrupt the cycle for 30s.

Connections: -> Projection (signal), <- The Dreaming Machine (contains), <- TouchDesigner (signal), <- Briony LoRA (training-lora)

### StreamDiffusion TOX
Type: td-internal | Tier: 1

Real-time img2img inference at 30fps

Connections: -> Output TOP (signal), <- TouchDesigner (contains), <- NDI In TOP (signal), <- Prompt Sequencer (signal)

### TouchDesigner
Type: software | Tier: 1

Integration hub. Autolume video via NDI, visitor prompts via OSC. Prompt Sequencer cycles 23 ecological prompts (26s each, 6s crossfade). StreamDiffusion runs inside as TOX.

Connections: -> StreamDiffusion (signal), -> NDI In TOP (contains), -> Kinect CHOP (contains), -> OSC In DAT (contains), -> Prompt Sequencer (contains), -> StreamDiffusion TOX (contains), -> Boids SOP (contains), -> Output TOP (contains), <- The Dreaming Machine (contains), <- Autolume (signal)
  ...and 1 more


## Visitor Dreams

Your words become dreams. Speak or type at the QR portal — your vision travels through GPT filtering, OSC, and TouchDesigner to the projection wall. The machine renders your dream back to you. Bidirectional: your words travel to the machine; its dreams travel back to the wall.


## Knowledge & Research

Reports, data, and Indigenous knowledge that ground the project. The Kwaxala model. Three-Eyed Seeing. The herring story.

### Three-Eyed Seeing
Type: concept | Tier: 0

Three-Eyed Seeing integrates Western scientific observation, Indigenous Traditional Knowledge, and direct perception from the land itself. Not a hierarchy but a braiding — each eye sees what the others cannot.

Connections: <- Knowledge & Research (contains)

### Darren Zal
Type: person | Tier: 1

Systems architect. Built training corpus, gallery server, data map, and knowledge pipeline.

Connections: -> Dreaming GAN (conceptual), -> Gallery Server (conceptual), <- Knowledge & Research (contains)

### Digital Ecologies: Mediating More-Than-Human Worlds
Type: report | Tier: 1

CC BY 4.0 — Turnbull, Searle, Anderson-Elliott, Giraud (eds.), Manchester University Press, 2024

Connections: -> Digital Ecologies (conceptual), <- Knowledge & Research (contains)

### Herring Data Science
Type: cluster-summary | Tier: 1

339 files of Pacific herring stock assessment, DFO catch data, population models, and statistical analysis. Shawn Anderson’s quantitative foundation for the herring thread.

Connections: <- Shawn Anderson (contains), <- Knowledge & Research (contains)

### Shawn Anderson
Type: person | Tier: 1

Herring data science package — 339 files of herring stock assessment analysis.

Connections: -> Herring Data Science (contains), <- Knowledge & Research (contains)

### The Living Salish Sea
Type: report | Tier: 1

Ecosystem health, Hornby stronghold, food web, conservation models

Connections: <- Knowledge & Research (contains)

### The Salish Sea Herring
Type: report | Tier: 1

DFO management, shifting baselines, Indigenous rights, trophic cascade

Connections: <- Knowledge & Research (contains)
